| [Badr City](/wiki/Badr,_Egypt "Badr, Egypt")                                  | 014600    | 31,299           | 17,449  | 13,850  |

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Religion")\]  
See also: [Religion in Egypt](/wiki/Religion_in_Egypt "Religion in Egypt")

The majority of Egypt and Cairo's population is Sunni Muslim.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-Britannica-2023-190)^^[\[189\]](#cite_note-US_Embassy_Egypt-2022-191)^ A significant Christian minority exists, among whom [Coptic Orthodox](/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox "Coptic Orthodox") are the majority.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-Britannica-2023-190)^^[\[189\]](#cite_note-US_Embassy_Egypt-2022-191)^ Precise numbers for each religious community in Egypt are not available and estimates vary.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-192)^ Other churches that have, or had, a presence in modern Cairo include the [Catholic Church](/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church") (including [Armenian Catholic](/wiki/Armenian_Catholic_Church "Armenian Catholic Church"), [Coptic Catholic](/wiki/Coptic_Catholic_Church "Coptic Catholic Church"), [Chaldean Catholic](/wiki/Chaldean_Catholic_Church "Chaldean Catholic Church"), [Syrian Catholic](/wiki/Syriac_Catholic_Church "Syriac Catholic Church"), and [Maronite](/wiki/Maronite_Church "Maronite Church")), the [Greek Orthodox Church](/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Patriarchate_of_Alexandria "Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Alexandria"), the [Evangelical Church of Egypt (Synod of the Nile)](/wiki/Evangelical_Church_of_Egypt_(Synod_of_the_Nile) "Evangelical Church of Egypt (Synod of the Nile)"), and some [Protestant](/wiki/Protestantism "Protestantism") churches.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-193)^ Cairo has been the seat of the Coptic Orthodox Church since the 12th century,^[\[192\]](#cite_note-194)^ and the [seat](/wiki/Seat_of_the_Coptic_Orthodox_Pope_of_Alexandria "Seat of the Coptic Orthodox Pope of Alexandria") of the [Coptic Orthodox Pope](/wiki/Pope_of_the_Coptic_Orthodox_Church "Pope of the Coptic Orthodox Church") is located in [Saint Mark's Coptic Orthodox Cathedral](/wiki/Saint_Mark%27s_Coptic_Orthodox_Cathedral "Saint Mark's Coptic Orthodox Cathedral").^[\[193\]](#cite_note-195)^ Until the 20th century, Cairo had a sizeable [Jewish community](/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Egypt "History of the Jews in Egypt"), but as of 2022 only three Jews were reported to be living in the city. A total of 12 [synagogues in Cairo](/wiki/Synagogues_in_Cairo "Synagogues in Cairo") still exist.^[\[194\]](#cite_note-Shawkat-2022-196)^{#cite_ref-Shawkat-2022_196-0}  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Economy")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg/170px-Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg)](/wiki/File:Talat_Harb_Square_-_Statue.jpg) Statue of [Talaat Pasha Harb](/wiki/Talaat_Harb "Talaat Harb"), the father of the modern [Egyptian economy](/wiki/Egyptian_economy "Egyptian economy"), in [Downtown Cairo](/wiki/Downtown_Cairo "Downtown Cairo") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG/220px-National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG)](/wiki/File:National_Bank_of_Egypt.JPG) The [NBE](/wiki/National_Bank_of_Egypt "National Bank of Egypt") towers as viewed from the Nile Informal economy in Cairo

Cairo's economy has traditionally been based on governmental institutions and services, with the modern productive sector expanding in the 20th century to include developments in textiles and food processing -- specifically the production of [sugar cane](/wiki/Sugar_cane "Sugar cane"). As of 2005, Egypt has the largest non-oil based GDP in the Arab world. ^[\[195\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21-197)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21_197-0}

Cairo accounts for 11% of Egypt's population and 22% of its economy (PPP). The majority of the nation's commerce is generated there, or passes through the city. The great majority of [publishing houses](/wiki/Publishing "Publishing") and media outlets and nearly all [film studios](/wiki/Movie_studio "Movie studio") are there, as are half of the nation's hospital beds and universities. This has fuelled rapid construction in the city, with one building in five being less than 15 years old.^[\[195\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21-197)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21_197-1}

This growth until recently surged well ahead of [city services](/wiki/Municipal_services "Municipal services"). Homes, roads, electricity, telephone and sewer services were all in short supply. Analysts trying to grasp the magnitude of the change coined terms like "hyper-urbanization".^[\[195\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21-197)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUN-Habitat201120-21_197-2}  

### Automobile manufacturers from Cairo {#Automobile_manufacturers_from_Cairo}

Infrastructure {#Infrastructure}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Infrastructure")\]  

### Health {#Health}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Health")\]  
See also: [List of hospitals in Egypt](/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Egypt "List of hospitals in Egypt")

Cairo, as well as neighbouring Giza, has been established as Egypt's main centre for medical treatment, and despite some exceptions, has the most advanced level of [medical care](/wiki/Health_care "Health care") in the country. Cairo's hospitals include the [JCI](/wiki/Joint_Commission "Joint Commission")-accredited [As-Salaam International Hospital](/w/index.php?title=As-Salaam_International_Hospital&action=edit&redlink=1 "As-Salaam International Hospital (page does not exist)"),^[\[203\]](#cite_note-205)^ [Ain Shams University](/wiki/Ain_Shams_University "Ain Shams University") Hospital,^[\[204\]](#cite_note-206)^ [Dar Al Fouad](/wiki/Dar_Al_Fouad "Dar Al Fouad"),^[\[205\]](#cite_note-207)^ [Nile Badrawi Hospital](/wiki/Nile_Badrawi_Hospital "Nile Badrawi Hospital"), [57357 Hospital](/wiki/57357_Hospital "57357 Hospital"),^[\[206\]](#cite_note-208)^ as well as [Qasr El Eyni Hospital](/wiki/Qasr_El_Eyni_Hospital "Qasr El Eyni Hospital").{#cite_ref-208}  

### Education {#Education}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Education")\]

[Greater Cairo](/wiki/Greater_Cairo "Greater Cairo") has long been the hub of education and educational services for Egypt and the region.

Today, Greater Cairo is the centre for many government offices governing the [Egyptian educational system](/wiki/Education_in_Egypt "Education in Egypt"), has the largest number of educational schools, and [higher education institutes](/wiki/Egyptian_universities "Egyptian universities") among other cities and governorates of Egypt.

**Some of the International Schools found in Cairo:**

Transport {#Transport}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Transport")\]  
Main article: [Transport in Cairo](/wiki/Transport_in_Cairo "Transport in Cairo")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/CairoIntlAirportTerminal3.jpg/203px-CairoIntlAirportTerminal3.jpg)](/wiki/File:CairoIntlAirportTerminal3.jpg)  
Façade of Terminal 3 at Cairo International Airport  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/CairoAirport-Terminal1.JPG/181px-CairoAirport-Terminal1.JPG)](/wiki/File:CairoAirport-Terminal1.JPG)  
Departures area of Cairo International Airport's Terminal 1

Cairo has an extensive road network, [rail system](/wiki/Rail_system "Rail system"), [subway system](/wiki/Rapid_transit "Rapid transit") and maritime services. Road transport is facilitated by personal vehicles, taxi cabs, privately owned public buses and [microbuses](/wiki/Microbus#Van_conversions "Microbus"). [Cairo International Airport](/wiki/Cairo_International_Airport "Cairo International Airport") is the country's largest airport and one of the busiest airports in Africa.^[\[207\]](#cite_note-209)^{#cite_ref-209}  

### Public transportation {#Public_transportation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Public transportation")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Ramses-Station.jpg/220px-Ramses-Station.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ramses-Station.jpg) The interior of [Ramses Station](/wiki/Ramses_Station "Ramses Station")

Cairo, specifically [Ramses Station](/wiki/Ramses_Station "Ramses Station"), is the centre of almost the entire Egyptian transportation network.^[\[208\]](#cite_note-TravelCairo-210)^{#cite_ref-TravelCairo_210-0}

The [Cairo Transportation Authority](/wiki/Cairo_Transportation_Authority "Cairo Transportation Authority") (CTA) manages Cairo's public transit. The subway system, the [Cairo Metro](/wiki/Cairo_Metro "Cairo Metro"), is a fast and efficient way of getting around Cairo. The metro network covers [Helwan](/wiki/Helwan "Helwan") and other suburbs. It can get very crowded during [rush hour](/wiki/Rush_hour "Rush hour"). Two train cars (the fourth and fifth ones) are reserved for women only, although women may ride in any car they want.

[Trams in Greater Cairo](/wiki/Trams_in_Greater_Cairo "Trams in Greater Cairo") and Cairo trolleybus were used as modes of transportation, but were closed in the 1970s everywhere except Heliopolis and Helwan. These were shut down in 2014, after the Egyptian Revolution.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-211)^{#cite_ref-211}

In 2017, plans to construct [two monorail systems](/wiki/Cairo_Monorail "Cairo Monorail") were announced, one linking [6th of October](/wiki/6th_of_October_(city) "6th of October (city)") to suburban [Giza](/wiki/Giza "Giza"), a distance of 35 km (22 mi), and the other linking [Nasr City](/wiki/Nasr_City "Nasr City") to [New Cairo](/wiki/New_Cairo "New Cairo"), a distance of 52 km (32 mi).^[\[210\]](#cite_note-212)^^[\[211\]](#cite_note-213)^{#cite_ref-213}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Cairo_Rapid_Transit_map.png/600px-Cairo_Rapid_Transit_map.png)](/wiki/File:Cairo_Rapid_Transit_map.png) Cairo Metro, LRT, BRT and monorail expansion plans  

### Roads {#Roads}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Roads")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846845880222%29.jpg/220px-Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846845880222%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cairo,_Egypt_(46845880222).jpg) [6th October Bridge](/wiki/6th_October_Bridge "6th October Bridge") in Cairo

Two trans-African automobile routes originate in Cairo: the [Cairo-Cape Town Highway](/wiki/Cairo-Cape_Town_Highway "Cairo-Cape Town Highway") and the [Cairo-Dakar Highway](/wiki/Cairo-Dakar_Highway "Cairo-Dakar Highway"). An extensive road network connects Cairo with other Egyptian cities and villages. There is a new [Ring Road](/wiki/Ring_road "Ring road") that surrounds the outskirts of the city, with exits that reach outer Cairo districts. There are flyovers and bridges, such as the [6th October Bridge](/wiki/6th_October_Bridge "6th October Bridge") that, when the traffic is not heavy, allow fast means of transportation from one side of the city to the other.^[\[208\]](#cite_note-TravelCairo-210)^{#cite_ref-TravelCairo_210-1}

Cairo traffic is known to be overwhelming and overcrowded.^[\[212\]](#cite_note-214)^ Traffic moves at a relatively fluid pace. Drivers tend to be aggressive, but are more courteous at junctions, taking turns going, with police aiding in [traffic control](/wiki/Road_traffic_control "Road traffic control") of some congested areas.^[\[208\]](#cite_note-TravelCairo-210)^{#cite_ref-TravelCairo_210-2}  

### Other forms of transport {#Other_forms_of_transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Other forms of transport")\]

* [Bolt](/wiki/Bolt_(company) "Bolt (company)")^[\[213\]](#cite_note-215)^{#cite_ref-215}
* Cairo Nile Ferry
* Cairo Taxi/Yellow Cab
* [Careem](/wiki/Careem "Careem")
* [DiDi](/wiki/DiDi "DiDi")^[\[214\]](#cite_note-216)^{#cite_ref-216}
* [Uber](/wiki/Uber "Uber")

### Cultural tourism in Egypt {#Cultural_tourism_in_Egypt}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Cultural tourism in Egypt")\]  
Main article: [Cultural tourism in Egypt](/wiki/Cultural_tourism_in_Egypt "Cultural tourism in Egypt")  

### Cairo Opera House {#Cairo_Opera_House}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Cairo Opera House")\]  
Main article: [Cairo Opera House](/wiki/Cairo_Opera_House "Cairo Opera House")

[President Mubarak](/wiki/President_Mubarak "President Mubarak") inaugurated the new Cairo Opera House of the Egyptian National Cultural Centres on 10 October 1988, 17 years after the Royal Opera House had been destroyed by fire. The National Cultural Centre was built with the help of [JICA](/wiki/JICA "JICA"), the Japan International Co-operation Agency and stands as a prominent feature for the [Japanese-Egyptian co-operation](/wiki/Egypt%E2%80%93Japan_relations "Egypt–Japan relations") and the friendship between the two nations.  

### Khedivial Opera House {#Khedivial_Opera_House}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Khedivial Opera House")\]  
Main article: [Khedivial Opera House](/wiki/Khedivial_Opera_House "Khedivial Opera House")

The [Khedivial Opera House](/wiki/Khedivial_Opera_House "Khedivial Opera House"), or Royal Opera House, was the original opera house in Cairo. It was dedicated on 1 November 1869 and burned down on 28 October 1971. After the original opera house was destroyed, Cairo was without an opera house for nearly two decades until the opening of the new Cairo Opera House in 1988.  

### Cairo International Film Festival {#Cairo_International_Film_Festival}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Cairo International Film Festival")\]  
Main article: [Cairo International Film Festival](/wiki/Cairo_International_Film_Festival "Cairo International Film Festival")

Cairo held its first international [film festival](/wiki/Film_festival "Film festival") 16 August 1976, when the first [Cairo International Film Festival](/wiki/Cairo_International_Film_Festival "Cairo International Film Festival") was launched by the Egyptian Association of Film Writers and Critics, headed by Kamal El-Mallakh. The Association ran the festival for seven years until 1983.^[\[215\]](#cite_note-217)^{#cite_ref-217}

This achievement lead to the President of the Festival again contacting the [FIAPF](/wiki/FIAPF "FIAPF") with the request that a competition should be included at the 1991 Festival. The request was granted.

In 1998, the Festival took place under the presidency of one of Egypt's leading actors, [Hussein Fahmy](/wiki/Hussein_Fahmy "Hussein Fahmy"), who was appointed by the [Minister of Culture](/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_(Egypt) "Ministry of Culture (Egypt)"), [Farouk Hosni](/wiki/Farouk_Hosny "Farouk Hosny"), after the death of Saad El-Din Wahba. Four years later, the journalist and writer Cherif El-Shoubashy became president.  

### Cairo Geniza {#Cairo_Geniza}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Cairo Geniza")\]  
Main article: [Cairo Geniza](/wiki/Cairo_Geniza "Cairo Geniza")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Solomon_Schechter_studying_the_fragments_of_the_Cairo_Genizah%2C_c._1898.jpg/220px-Solomon_Schechter_studying_the_fragments_of_the_Cairo_Genizah%2C_c._1898.jpg)](/wiki/File:Solomon_Schechter_studying_the_fragments_of_the_Cairo_Genizah,_c._1898.jpg) [Solomon Schechter](/wiki/Solomon_Schechter "Solomon Schechter") at work in Cambridge University Library, studying the fragments of the [Cairo Geniza](/wiki/Cairo_Geniza "Cairo Geniza"),  1898

The Cairo Geniza is an accumulation of almost 200,000 Jewish manuscripts that were found in the *[genizah](/wiki/Genizah "Genizah")* of the [Ben Ezra Synagogue](/wiki/Ben_Ezra_Synagogue "Ben Ezra Synagogue") (built 882) of Fustat, Egypt (now Old Cairo), the Basatin cemetery east of Old Cairo, and a number of old documents that were bought in Cairo in the later 19th century. These documents were written from about 870 to 1880 AD and have been archived in various American and European libraries. The Taylor-Schechter collection in the [University of Cambridge](/wiki/University_of_Cambridge "University of Cambridge") runs to 140,000 manuscripts; a further 40,000 manuscripts are housed at the [Jewish Theological Seminary of America](/wiki/Jewish_Theological_Seminary_of_America "Jewish Theological Seminary of America").  

### Food {#Food}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Food")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Down_Town_Cairo_snack.jpg/220px-Down_Town_Cairo_snack.jpg)](/wiki/File:Down_Town_Cairo_snack.jpg) Down Town Cairo Snack

The majority of Cairenes make food for themselves and make use of local produce markets.^[\[216\]](#cite_note-Planet-2020-218)^ The restaurant scene includes [Arab cuisine](/wiki/Arab_cuisine "Arab cuisine") and [Middle Eastern cuisine](/wiki/Middle_Eastern_cuisine "Middle Eastern cuisine"), including local staples such as *[koshary](/wiki/Koshary "Koshary")* . The city's most exclusive restaurants are typically concentrated in [Zamalek](/wiki/Zamalek "Zamalek") and around the luxury hotels lining the shore of the Nile near the [Garden City](/wiki/Garden_City,_Cairo "Garden City, Cairo") district. Influence from modern [western](/wiki/Western_world "Western world") society is also evident, with American chains such as [McDonald's](/wiki/McDonald%27s "McDonald's"), [Arby's](/wiki/Arby%27s "Arby's"), [Pizza Hut](/wiki/Pizza_Hut "Pizza Hut"), [Subway](/wiki/Subway_(restaurant) "Subway (restaurant)"), and [Kentucky Fried Chicken](/wiki/KFC "KFC") being easy to find in central areas.^[\[216\]](#cite_note-Planet-2020-218)^{#cite_ref-Planet-2020_218-1}  

Sports {#Sports}
----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg/220px-Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg)](/wiki/File:Crowd_in_Cairo_Stadium.jpg) [Cairo International Stadium](/wiki/Cairo_International_Stadium "Cairo International Stadium") with 75,100 seats

[Football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") is the most popular sport in Egypt,^[\[217\]](#cite_note-219)^ and Cairo has sporting teams that compete in national and regional leagues, most notably [Al Ahly](/wiki/Al_Ahly_SC "Al Ahly SC") and [Zamalek SC](/wiki/Zamalek_SC "Zamalek SC"), who were the [CAF](/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football "Confederation of African Football") first and second African clubs of the 20th century. The annual match between Al Ahly and El Zamalek is one of the most watched sports events in Egypt. The teams form the major rivalry of Egyptian football. They play their home games at [Cairo International Stadium](/wiki/Cairo_International_Stadium "Cairo International Stadium"), which is the second largest stadium in Egypt, as well as the largest in Cairo.{#cite_ref-219}

The Cairo International Stadium was built in 1960. Its multi-purpose sports complex houses the main football stadium, an [indoor stadium](/wiki/Cairo_Stadium_Indoor_Halls_Complex "Cairo Stadium Indoor Halls Complex"), satellite fields that hold regional and continental games, including the [African Games](/wiki/All-Africa_Games "All-Africa Games"), U17 Football World Championship and the [2006 Africa Cup of Nations](/wiki/2006_Africa_Cup_of_Nations "2006 Africa Cup of Nations"). Egypt later won the competition and the next edition in Ghana (2008) making the Egyptian and Ghanaian national teams the only to win the African Nations Cup back to back. Egypt won the title for a record six times in the history of African Continental Competition. This was followed by a third consecutive win in Angola in 2010, making Egypt the only country with a record 3-consecutive and 7-total Continental Football Competition winner. As of 2021, Egypt's national team is ranked #46 in the world by FIFA.^[\[218\]](#cite_note-220)^{#cite_ref-220}

Cairo failed at the applicant stage when bidding for the [2008 Summer Olympics](/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics "2008 Summer Olympics"), which was hosted in Beijing.^[\[219\]](#cite_note-221)^ However, Cairo did host the [2007 Pan Arab Games](/wiki/2007_Pan_Arab_Games "2007 Pan Arab Games").^[\[220\]](#cite_note-222)^{#cite_ref-222}

There are other sports teams in the city that participate in several sports including [Gezira Sporting Club](/wiki/Gezira_Sporting_Club "Gezira Sporting Club"), el Shams Club, [Shooting Club](/wiki/Egyptian_Shooting_Club "Egyptian Shooting Club"), [Heliopolis Sporting Club](/wiki/Heliopolis_Sporting_Club "Heliopolis Sporting Club"), and several smaller clubs. There are new sports clubs in the area of New Cairo (one hour far from Cairo's downtown), these are Al Zohour sporting club, Wadi Degla sporting club and Platinum Club.^[\[221\]](#cite_note-223)^{#cite_ref-223}

Most of the sports federations of the country are located in the city suburbs, including the [Egyptian Football Association](/wiki/Egyptian_Football_Association "Egyptian Football Association").^[\[222\]](#cite_note-224)^ The headquarters of the [Confederation of African Football](/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football "Confederation of African Football") (CAF) was previously located in Cairo, before relocating to its new headquarters in [6 October City](/wiki/6th_of_October_City "6th of October City"), a small city away from Cairo's crowded districts. In 2008, the Egyptian Rugby Federation was officially formed and granted membership into the [International Rugby Board](/wiki/International_Rugby_Board "International Rugby Board").^[\[223\]](#cite_note-225)^{#cite_ref-225}

Egypt is internationally known for the excellence of its squash players who excel in professional and junior divisions.^[\[224\]](#cite_note-226)^ Egypt has seven players in the top ten of the PSA men's world rankings, and three in the women's top ten. [Mohamed El Shorbagy](/wiki/Mohamed_El_Shorbagy "Mohamed El Shorbagy") held the world number one position for more than a year. [Nour El Sherbini](/wiki/Nour_El_Sherbini "Nour El Sherbini") has won the Women's World Championship twice and been women's world number one. On 30 April 2016, she became the youngest woman to win the Women's World Championship. In 2017 she retained her title.{#cite_ref-226}

Cairo is the official end point of [Cross Egypt Challenge](/wiki/Cross_Egypt_Challenge "Cross Egypt Challenge") where its route ends yearly in the most sacred place in Egypt, under the [Great Pyramids of Giza](/wiki/Great_Pyramids_of_Giza "Great Pyramids of Giza") with a huge trophy-giving ceremony.^[\[225\]](#cite_note-227)^{#cite_ref-227}  

Cityscape and landmarks {#Cityscape_and_landmarks}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Cityscape and landmarks")\]  
[![Cityscape of the banks of the Nile.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846846056782%29.jpg/1200px-Cairo%2C_Egypt_%2846846056782%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cairo,_Egypt_(46846056782).jpg "Cityscape of the banks of the Nile.")  
[](/wiki/File:Cairo,_Egypt_(46846056782).jpg "File:Cairo, Egypt (46846056782).jpg")
[Cityscape](/wiki/Cityscape "Cityscape") of the banks of the Nile.  

### Tahrir Square {#Tahrir_Square}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Tahrir Square")\]  
Main article: [Tahrir Square](/wiki/Tahrir_Square "Tahrir Square")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/TahrirSQ-2020%282%29.jpg/220px-TahrirSQ-2020%282%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:TahrirSQ-2020(2).jpg) View of [Tahrir Square](/wiki/Tahrir_Square "Tahrir Square") (in 2020)

Tahrir Square was founded during the mid 19th century with the establishment of modern downtown Cairo. It was first named Ismailia Square, after the 19th-century ruler Khedive Ismail, who commissioned the new downtown district's 'Paris on the Nile' design. After the [Egyptian Revolution of 1919](/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1919 "Egyptian Revolution of 1919") the square became widely known as Tahrir (Liberation) Square, though it was not officially renamed as such until after the [1952 Revolution](/wiki/Egyptian_Revolution_of_1952 "Egyptian Revolution of 1952") which eliminated the monarchy. Several notable buildings surround the square including, the American University in Cairo's downtown campus, the [Mogamma](/wiki/Mogamma "Mogamma") governmental administrative Building, the headquarters of the [Arab League](/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League"), the Nile Ritz Carlton Hotel, and the [Egyptian Museum](/wiki/Egyptian_Museum "Egyptian Museum"). Being at the heart of Cairo, the square witnessed several major protests over the years. However, the most notable event in the square was being the focal point of the [2011 Egyptian Revolution](/wiki/2011_Egyptian_Revolution "2011 Egyptian Revolution") against former president Hosni Mubarak.^[\[226\]](#cite_note-228)^ In 2020 the government completed the erection of a new monument in the center of the square featuring an ancient [obelisk](/wiki/Obelisk "Obelisk") from the reign of [Ramses II](/wiki/Ramesses_II "Ramesses II"), originally unearthed at [Tanis](/wiki/Tanis "Tanis") (San al-Hagar) in 2019, and four ram-headed [sphinx](/wiki/Sphinx "Sphinx") statues moved from [Karnak](/wiki/Karnak "Karnak").^[\[227\]](#cite_note-Michaelson-2020-229)^^[\[228\]](#cite_note-230)^^[\[229\]](#cite_note-231)^{#cite_ref-231}  

### Egyptian Museum {#Egyptian_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Egyptian Museum")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_03.jpg/220px-Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_03.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kairo_%C3%84gyptisches_Museum_03.jpg) Main entrance of the [Egyptian Museum](/wiki/Egyptian_Museum "Egyptian Museum"), located at Tahrir Square

The Museum of Egyptian Antiquities, known commonly as the Egyptian Museum, is home to the most extensive collection of ancient Egyptian antiquities in the world. It has 136,000 items on display, with many more hundreds of thousands in its basement storerooms. Among the collections on display are the finds from the [tomb of Tutankhamun](/wiki/KV62 "KV62").^[\[230\]](#cite_note-232)^{#cite_ref-232}  

#### Grand Egyptian Museum {#Grand_Egyptian_Museum}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Grand Egyptian Museum")\]  
Main article: [Grand Egyptian Museum](/wiki/Grand_Egyptian_Museum "Grand Egyptian Museum")

Much of the collection of the Museum of Egyptian Antiquities, including the Tutankhamun collection, are slated to be moved to the new [Grand Egyptian Museum](/wiki/Grand_Egyptian_Museum "Grand Egyptian Museum"), under construction in [Giza](/wiki/Giza "Giza") and was due to open by the end of 2020.^[\[231\]](#cite_note-233)^^[\[232\]](#cite_note-234)^{#cite_ref-234}  

### Cairo Tower {#Cairo_Tower}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Cairo Tower")\]  
Main article: [Cairo Tower](/wiki/Cairo_Tower "Cairo Tower")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Cairotower.jpg/170px-Cairotower.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cairotower.jpg) [Cairo Tower](/wiki/Cairo_Tower "Cairo Tower") at night

The Cairo Tower is a free-standing tower with a revolving restaurant at the top. It is one of Cairo's landmarks and provides a bird's eye view of the city to the restaurant patrons. It stands in the Zamalek district on Gezira Island in the Nile River, in the city centre. At 187 m (614 ft), it is 44 m (144 ft) higher than the Great Pyramid of Giza, which stands some 15 km (9 mi) to the southwest.^[\[233\]](#cite_note-235)^{#cite_ref-235}  

### Old Cairo {#Old_Cairo}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Old Cairo")\]  
Main articles: [Old Cairo](/wiki/Old_Cairo "Old Cairo") and [Coptic Cairo](/wiki/Coptic_Cairo "Coptic Cairo")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg/220px-Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg)](/wiki/File:Hanging_Church_Cairo.jpg) The [Hanging Church](/wiki/Hanging_Church "Hanging Church") in [Old Cairo](/wiki/Old_Cairo "Old Cairo")

This area of Cairo is so-named as it contains the remains of the ancient Roman fortress of Babylon and also overlaps the original site of Fustat, the first Arab settlement in Egypt (7th century AD) and the predecessor of later Cairo. The area includes Coptic Cairo, which holds a high concentration of old Christian churches such as the [Hanging Church](/wiki/Hanging_Church "Hanging Church"), the [Greek Orthodox Church of St. George](/wiki/Church_of_St._George_(Cairo) "Church of St. George (Cairo)"), and other Christian or Coptic buildings, most of which are located in an enclave on the site of the ancient Roman fortress. It is also the location of the [Coptic Museum](/wiki/Coptic_Museum "Coptic Museum"), which showcases the history of [Coptic art](/wiki/Coptic_art "Coptic art") from Greco-Roman to Islamic times, and of the [Ben Ezra Synagogue](/wiki/Ben_Ezra_Synagogue "Ben Ezra Synagogue"), the oldest and best-known [synagogue](/wiki/Synagogue "Synagogue") in Cairo, where the important collection of Geniza documents were discovered in the 19th century.^[\[234\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200843-236)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams200843_236-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/010112_00001_Koptisches_Viertel%2C_Kairo.jpg/220px-010112_00001_Koptisches_Viertel%2C_Kairo.jpg)](/wiki/File:010112_00001_Koptisches_Viertel,_Kairo.jpg) Cemetery in Coptic Cairo

To the north of this Coptic enclave is the Amr ibn al-'As Mosque, the first mosque in Egypt and the most important religious centre of what was formerly Fustat, founded in 642 AD right after the Arab conquest but rebuilt many times since.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200839-237)^ A part of the former city of Fustat has also been excavated to the east of the mosque and of the Coptic enclave,^[\[236\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGabravan_LoonReifSwelim2013275–279-238)^^[\[237\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams201847–48-239)^^[\[238\]](#cite_note-240)^ although the archeological site is threatened by encroaching construction and modern development.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams201847–48-239)^^[\[239\]](#cite_note-241)^ To the northwest of Babylon Fortress and the mosque is the Monastery of Saint Mercurius (or *Dayr Abu Sayfayn* ), an important and historic Coptic religious complex consisting of the [Church of Saint Mercurius](/wiki/Saint_Mercurius_Church_in_Coptic_Cairo "Saint Mercurius Church in Coptic Cairo"), the Church of Saint Shenute, and the Church of the Virgin (also known as *al-Damshiriya* ).^[\[240\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGabravan_LoonReifSwelim2013178-242)^ Several other historic churches are also situated to the south of Babylon Fortress.^[\[241\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGabravan_LoonReifSwelim2013230-243)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGabravan_LoonReifSwelim2013230_243-0}  

### Islamic Cairo {#Islamic_Cairo}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Islamic Cairo")\]  
Main article: [Islamic Cairo](/wiki/Islamic_Cairo "Islamic Cairo")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Al-Azhar_%28inside%29_2006.jpg/170px-Al-Azhar_%28inside%29_2006.jpg)](/wiki/File:Al-Azhar_(inside)_2006.jpg) Al-Azhar Mosque, view of Fatimid-era courtyard and Mamluk minarets [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg/220px-El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg)](/wiki/File:El-Moez_Street-Old_Cairo-Egypt.jpg) [Al-Muizz Street](/wiki/Muizz_Street "Muizz Street") in [Islamic Cairo](/wiki/Islamic_Cairo "Islamic Cairo") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg/220px-%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg)](/wiki/File:%D9%85%D8%B5%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%82%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%85%D9%87_..%D8%AD%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AE%D8%A7%D9%86%D9%83%D9%87.jpg) [Mosque-Madrasa of Sultan Hassan](/wiki/Mosque-Madrasa_of_Sultan_Hassan "Mosque-Madrasa of Sultan Hassan") and the [al-Rifa'i Mosque](/wiki/Al-Rifa%27i_Mosque "Al-Rifa'i Mosque"), seen from the Citadel

Cairo holds one of the greatest concentrations of historical monuments of [Islamic architecture](/wiki/Islamic_architecture "Islamic architecture") in the world.^[\[242\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_March_2022]]<sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i>[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|<span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&#32;(March_2022)">page&nbsp;needed</span>]]</i>&#93;</sup>-244)^ The areas around the old walled city and around the Citadel are characterized by hundreds of mosques, tombs, [madrasas](/wiki/Madrasas "Madrasas"), mansions, [caravanserais](/wiki/Caravanserais "Caravanserais"), and fortifications dating from the Islamic era and are often referred to as "[Islamic Cairo](/wiki/Islamic_Cairo "Islamic Cairo")", especially in English travel literature.^[\[243\]](#cite_note-245)^ It is also the location of several important religious shrines such as the [al-Hussein Mosque](/wiki/Al-Hussein_Mosque "Al-Hussein Mosque") (whose shrine is believed to hold the head of [Husayn ibn Ali](/wiki/Husayn_ibn_Ali "Husayn ibn Ali")), the Mausoleum of Imam [al-Shafi'i](/wiki/Al-Shafi%27i "Al-Shafi'i") (founder of the [Shafi'i](/wiki/Shafi%27i "Shafi'i") *[madhhab](/wiki/Madhhab "Madhhab")* , one of the primary schools of thought in Sunni [Islamic jurisprudence](/wiki/Islamic_jurisprudence "Islamic jurisprudence")), the [Tomb of Sayyida Ruqayya](/wiki/Mashhad_of_Sayyida_Ruqayya "Mashhad of Sayyida Ruqayya"), the [Mosque of Sayyida Nafisa](/wiki/Al-Sayeda_Nafeesah_Mosque "Al-Sayeda Nafeesah Mosque"), and others.^[\[244\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008-246)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008_246-0}

The first mosque in Egypt was the Mosque of Amr ibn al-As in what was formerly Fustat, the first Arab-Muslim settlement in the area. However, the Mosque of Ibn Tulun is the oldest mosque that still retains its original form and is a rare example of Abbasid architecture from the [classical period of Islamic civilization](/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age"). It was built in 876--879 AD in a style inspired by the Abbasid capital of [Samarra](/wiki/Samarra "Samarra") in Iraq.^[\[245\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200850–54-247)^ It is one of the largest mosques in Cairo and is often cited as one of the most beautiful.^[\[246\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams200850-248)^^[\[247\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201287-249)^ Another Abbasid construction, the [Nilometer](/wiki/Nilometer "Nilometer") on Roda Island, is the oldest original structure in Cairo, built in 862 AD. It was designed to measure the level of the Nile, which was important for agricultural and administrative purposes.^[\[248\]](#cite_note-250)^{#cite_ref-250}

The settlement that was formally named Cairo (Arabic: *al-Qahira* ) was founded to the northeast of Fustat in 959 AD by the victorious Fatimid army. The Fatimids built it as a separate palatial city which contained their palaces and institutions of government. It was enclosed by a circuit of walls, which were rebuilt in stone in the late 11th century AD by the vizier Badr al-Gamali,^[\[249\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond199362-251)^ parts of which survive today at Bab Zuwayla in the south and Bab al-Futuh and Bab al-Nasr in the north. Among the extant monuments from the Fatimid era are the large [Mosque of al-Hakim](/wiki/Al-Hakim_Mosque "Al-Hakim Mosque"), the [Aqmar Mosque](/wiki/Aqmar_Mosque "Aqmar Mosque"), [Juyushi Mosque](/wiki/Juyushi_Mosque "Juyushi Mosque"), [Lulua Mosque](/wiki/Lulua_Mosque "Lulua Mosque"), and the [Mosque of Al-Salih Tala'i](/wiki/Al-Salih_Tala%27i_Mosque "Al-Salih Tala'i Mosque").^[\[250\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBehrens-Abouseif199258–77-252)^^[\[244\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008-246)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008_246-1}

One of the most important and lasting institutions founded in the Fatimid period was the Mosque of al-Azhar, founded in 970 AD, which competes with the [Qarawiyyin](/wiki/Qarawiyyin "Qarawiyyin") in [Fes](/wiki/Fes "Fes") for the title of oldest university in the world.^[\[251\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008169-253)^ Today, al-Azhar University is the foremost Center of Islamic learning in the world and one of Egypt's largest universities with campuses across the country.^[\[251\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008169-253)^ The mosque itself retains significant Fatimid elements but has been added to and expanded in subsequent centuries, notably by the Mamluk sultans Qaytbay and al-Ghuri and by Abd al-Rahman Katkhuda in the 18th century.^[\[252\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBehrens-Abouseif199262-254)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBehrens-Abouseif199262_254-0}

The most prominent architectural heritage of medieval Cairo, however, dates from the Mamluk period, from 1250 to 1517 AD. The Mamluk sultans and elites were eager patrons of religious and scholarly life, commonly building religious or funerary complexes whose functions could include a mosque, madrasa, [khanqah](/wiki/Khanqah "Khanqah") (for [Sufis](/wiki/Sufis "Sufis")), a [sabil](/wiki/Sebil_(fountain) "Sebil (fountain)") (water dispensary), and a mausoleum for themselves and their families.^[\[79\]](#cite_note-Behrens-2007-81)^ Among the best-known examples of Mamluk monuments in Cairo are the huge [Mosque-Madrasa of Sultan Hasan](/wiki/Mosque-Madrasa_of_Sultan_Hasan "Mosque-Madrasa of Sultan Hasan"), the [Mosque of Amir al-Maridani](/wiki/Mosque_of_Amir_al-Maridani "Mosque of Amir al-Maridani"), the [Mosque of Sultan al-Mu'ayyad](/wiki/Mosque_of_Sultan_al-Muayyad "Mosque of Sultan al-Muayyad") (whose twin minarets were built above the gate of Bab Zuwayla), the [Sultan Al-Ghuri complex](/wiki/Sultan_Al-Ghuri_Complex "Sultan Al-Ghuri Complex"), the [funerary complex of Sultan Qaytbay](/wiki/Complex_of_Sultan_al-Ashraf_Qaytbay "Complex of Sultan al-Ashraf Qaytbay") in the [Northern Cemetery](/wiki/City_of_the_Dead_(Cairo) "City of the Dead (Cairo)"), and the trio of monuments in the [Bayn al-Qasrayn](/wiki/Bayn_al-Qasrayn "Bayn al-Qasrayn") area comprising the [complex of Sultan al-Mansur Qalawun](/wiki/Qalawun_complex "Qalawun complex"), the [Madrasa of al-Nasir Muhammad](/wiki/Madrassa_of_Al-Nasir_Muhammad "Madrassa of Al-Nasir Muhammad"), and the [Madrasa of Sultan Barquq](/wiki/Madrasa_of_Sultan_Barquq "Madrasa of Sultan Barquq"). Some mosques include [spolia](/wiki/Spolia "Spolia") (often columns or [capitals](/wiki/Capital_(architecture) "Capital (architecture)")) from earlier buildings built by the [Romans](/wiki/Ancient_Rome "Ancient Rome"), [Byzantines](/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"), or [Copts](/wiki/Copts "Copts").^[\[242\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_March_2022]]<sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i>[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|<span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&#32;(March_2022)">page&nbsp;needed</span>]]</i>&#93;</sup>-244)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008[[Category:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_March_2022]]<sup_class="noprint_Inline-Template_"_style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i>[[Wikipedia:Citing_sources|<span_title="This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears.&#32;(March_2022)">page&nbsp;needed</span>]]</i>&#93;</sup>_244-1}

The Mamluks, and the later Ottomans, also built *wikala* s or caravanserais to house merchants and goods due to the important role of trade and commerce in Cairo's economy.^[\[253\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond199390–97-255)^ Still intact today is the [Wikala al-Ghuri](/wiki/Wikala_of_Al-Ghuri "Wikala of Al-Ghuri"), which today hosts regular performances by the Al-[Tannoura](/wiki/Tannoura "Tannoura") Egyptian Heritage Dance Troupe.^[\[254\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201281-256)^ The [Khan al-Khalili](/wiki/Khan_el-Khalili "Khan el-Khalili") is a commercial hub which also integrated caravanserais (also known as *khan* s).^[\[255\]](#cite_note-Denoix-1999a-257)^{#cite_ref-Denoix-1999a_257-0}  

### Citadel of Cairo {#Citadel_of_Cairo}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Citadel of Cairo")\]  
Main article: [Cairo Citadel](/wiki/Cairo_Citadel "Cairo Citadel")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Flickr_-_HuTect_ShOts_-_Citadel_of_Salah_El.Din_and_Masjid_Muhammad_Ali_%D9%82%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A9_%D8%B5%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%AD_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A3%D9%8A%D9%88%D8%A8%D9%8A_%D9%88%D9%85%D8%B3%D8%AC%D8%AF_%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D8%B9%D9%84%D9%8A_-_Cairo_-_Egypt_-_17_04_2010_%284%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg)](/wiki/File:Flickr_-_HuTect_ShOts_-_Citadel_of_Salah_El.Din_and_Masjid_Muhammad_Ali_%D9%82%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%A9_%D8%B5%D9%84%D8%A7%D8%AD_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%8A%D9%86_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A3%D9%8A%D9%88%D8%A8%D9%8A_%D9%88%D9%85%D8%B3%D8%AC%D8%AF_%D9%85%D8%AD%D9%85%D8%AF_%D8%B9%D9%84%D9%8A_-_Cairo_-_Egypt_-_17_04_2010_(4).jpg) The Citadel of Cairo, with the [Mosque of Muhammad Ali](/wiki/Mosque_of_Muhammad_Ali "Mosque of Muhammad Ali")

The Citadel is a fortified enclosure begun by [Salah al-Din](/wiki/Saladin "Saladin") in 1176 AD on an outcrop of the [Muqattam Hills](/wiki/Muqatam "Muqatam") as part of a large defensive system to protect both Cairo to the north and [Fustat](/wiki/Fustat "Fustat") to the southwest.^[\[253\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond199390–97-255)^ It was the centre of Egyptian government and residence of its rulers until 1874, when [Khedive Isma'il](/wiki/Isma%27il_Pasha "Isma'il Pasha") moved to ['Abdin Palace](/wiki/Abdeen_Palace "Abdeen Palace").^[\[256\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008221-258)^ It is still occupied by the military today, but is now open as a tourist attraction comprising, notably, the [National Military Museum](/wiki/Egyptian_National_Military_Museum "Egyptian National Military Museum"), the 14th century [Mosque of al-Nasir Muhammad](/wiki/Al-Nasir_Muhammad_Mosque "Al-Nasir Muhammad Mosque"), and the 19th century [Mosque of Muhammad Ali](/wiki/Mosque_of_Muhammad_Ali "Mosque of Muhammad Ali") which commands a dominant position on Cairo's skyline.^[\[257\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2018259–272-259)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2018259–272_259-0}  

### Khan el-Khalili {#Khan_el-Khalili}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Khan el-Khalili")\]  
Main article: [Khan el-Khalili](/wiki/Khan_el-Khalili "Khan el-Khalili")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Khan_el-Khalili%2C_Old_Cairo%2C_al-Q%C4%81hirah%2C_CG%2C_EGY_%2840944894033%29.jpg/220px-Khan_el-Khalili%2C_Old_Cairo%2C_al-Q%C4%81hirah%2C_CG%2C_EGY_%2840944894033%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Khan_el-Khalili,_Old_Cairo,_al-Q%C4%81hirah,_CG,_EGY_(40944894033).jpg) A medieval gateway in [Khan al-Khalili](/wiki/Khan_el-Khalili "Khan el-Khalili")

Khan el-Khalili is an ancient [bazaar](/wiki/Bazaar "Bazaar"), or marketplace adjacent to the [Al-Hussein Mosque](/wiki/Al-Hussein_Mosque "Al-Hussein Mosque"). It dates back to 1385, when Amir Jarkas el-Khalili built a large caravanserai, or khan. (A caravanserai is a hotel for traders, and usually the focal point for any surrounding area.) This original caravanserai building was demolished by [Sultan al-Ghuri](/wiki/Qansuh_al-Ghuri "Qansuh al-Ghuri"), who rebuilt it as a new commercial complex in the early 16th century, forming the basis for the network of souqs existing today.^[\[258\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaymond1993179-260)^ Many medieval elements remain today, including the ornate Mamluk-style gateways.^[\[259\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2008179-261)^ Today, the Khan el-Khalili is a major tourist attraction and popular stop for tour groups.^[\[260\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201274–75-262)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO'Neill_et_al201274–75_262-0}  

Society {#Society}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Society")\]

In the present day, Cairo is a heavily urbanized city. Because of the influx of people into the city, lone standing houses are rare, and apartment buildings accommodate for the limited space and abundance of people. Single detached houses are usually owned by the wealthy.^[\[261\]](#cite_note-february-263)^ Formal education is also seen as important, with twelve years of standard formal education. Cairenes can take a standardized test similar to the [SAT](/wiki/SAT "SAT") to be accepted to an institution of higher learning, but most children do not finish school and opt to pick up a trade to enter the work force.^[\[261\]](#cite_note-february-263)^ Egypt still struggles with [poverty](/wiki/Poverty "Poverty"), with almost half the population living on $2 or less a day.^[\[262\]](#cite_note-264)^{#cite_ref-264}  

### Women's rights {#Women.27s_rights}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Women's rights")\]  
Main article: [Women in Egypt](/wiki/Women_in_Egypt "Women in Egypt")

The civil rights movement for women in Cairo -- and by extent, Egypt -- has been a struggle for years. Women are reported to face constant discrimination, sexual harassment, and abuse throughout Cairo. A 2013 [UN](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") study found that over 99% of [Egyptian women](/wiki/Women_in_Egypt "Women in Egypt") reported experiencing sexual harassment at some point in their lives.^[\[263\]](#cite_note-265)^ The problem has persisted in spite of new national laws since 2014 defining and criminalizing sexual harassment.^[\[264\]](#cite_note-266)^ The situation is so severe that in 2017, Cairo was named by one poll as the most dangerous [megacity](/wiki/Megacity "Megacity") for women in the world.^[\[265\]](#cite_note-267)^ In 2020, the social media account "Assault Police" began to name and shame perpetrators of violence against women, in an effort to dissuade potential offenders.^[\[266\]](#cite_note-268)^ The account was founded by student [Nadeen Ashraf](/wiki/Nadeen_Ashraf "Nadeen Ashraf"), who is credited for instigating an iteration of the [#MeToo movement](/wiki/Me_Too_movement "Me Too movement") in Egypt.^[\[267\]](#cite_note-269)^{#cite_ref-269}  

Pollution {#Pollution}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Pollution")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/NilPollution.jpg/220px-NilPollution.jpg)](/wiki/File:NilPollution.jpg) Smog in Cairo [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Cairo_Traffic.jpg/220px-Cairo_Traffic.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cairo_Traffic.jpg) Traffic in Cairo

The [air pollution](/wiki/Air_pollution "Air pollution") in Cairo is a matter of serious concern. Greater Cairo's volatile [aromatic hydrocarbon](/wiki/Aromatic_hydrocarbon "Aromatic hydrocarbon") levels are higher than many other similar cities.^[\[268\]](#cite_note-270)^ Air quality measurements in Cairo have also been recording dangerous levels of [lead](/wiki/Lead "Lead"), [carbon dioxide](/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide"), [sulphur dioxide](/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide "Sulfur dioxide"), and [suspended particulate matter](/wiki/Suspended_solids "Suspended solids") concentrations due to decades of unregulated [vehicle emissions](/wiki/Vehicle_emissions_control "Vehicle emissions control"), urban industrial operations, and chaff and trash burning. There are over 4,500,000 cars on the streets of Cairo, 60% of which are over 10 years old, and therefore lack modern emission cutting features. Cairo has a very poor dispersion factor because of its lack of rain and its layout of tall buildings and narrow streets, which create a bowl effect.^[\[269\]](#cite_note-271)^{#cite_ref-271}

In recent years, a black cloud (as Egyptians refer to it) of [smog](/wiki/Smog "Smog") has appeared over Cairo every autumn due to [temperature inversion](/wiki/Inversion_(meteorology) "Inversion (meteorology)"). Smog causes serious respiratory diseases and eye irritations for the city's citizens. Tourists who are not familiar with such high levels of pollution must take extra care.^[\[270\]](#cite_note-272)^{#cite_ref-272}

Cairo also has many unregistered lead and [copper](/wiki/Copper "Copper") [smelters](/wiki/Smelter "Smelter") which heavily pollute the city. The results of this has been a permanent haze over the city with [particulate matter](/wiki/Particulate_matter "Particulate matter") in the air reaching over three times normal levels. It is estimated that 10,000 to 25,000 people a year in Cairo die due to air pollution-related diseases. Lead has been shown to cause harm to the [central nervous system](/wiki/Central_nervous_system "Central nervous system") and neurotoxicity particularly in children.^[\[271\]](#cite_note-273)^ In 1995, the first environmental acts were introduced and the situation has seen some improvement with 36 air monitoring stations and [emissions tests](/wiki/Emissions_testing "Emissions testing") on cars. Twenty thousand buses have also been commissioned to the city to improve congestion levels, which are very high.^[\[272\]](#cite_note-274)^{#cite_ref-274}

The city also suffers from a high level of land pollution. Cairo produces 10,000 tons of waste material each day, 4,000 tons of which is not [collected](/wiki/Waste_collection "Waste collection") or [managed](/wiki/Waste_management "Waste management"). This is a huge health hazard, and the Egyptian Government is looking for ways to combat this. The Cairo Cleaning and Beautification Agency was founded to collect and recycle the waste; they work with the [Zabbaleen](/wiki/Zabbaleen "Zabbaleen") community that has been collecting and recycling Cairo's waste since the turn of the 20th century and live in an area known locally as [Manshiyat naser](/wiki/Manshiyat_naser "Manshiyat naser").^[\[273\]](#cite_note-275)^ Both are working together to pick up as much waste as possible within the city limits, though it remains a pressing problem.{#cite_ref-275}

[Water pollution](/wiki/Water_pollution "Water pollution") is also a serious problem in the city as the [sewer system](/wiki/Sanitary_sewer "Sanitary sewer") tends to fail and overflow. On occasion, [sewage](/wiki/Sewage "Sewage") has escaped onto the streets to create a health hazard. This problem is hoped to be solved by a new sewer system funded by the [European Union](/wiki/European_Union "European Union"), which could cope with the demand of the city.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ The dangerously high levels of [mercury](/wiki/Mercury_(element) "Mercury (element)") in the city's water system has [global health](/wiki/Global_health "Global health") officials concerned over related health risks.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^  

International relations {#International_relations}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: International relations")\]

The [Headquarters of the Arab League](/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_Arab_League "Headquarters of the Arab League") is located at [Tahrir Square](/wiki/Tahrir_Square "Tahrir Square") in downtown Cairo.  

### Twin towns -- sister cities {#Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities")\]  
See also: [List of twin towns and sister cities in Egypt](/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Egypt "List of twin towns and sister cities in Egypt")

Cairo is [twinned](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city") with:^[\[274\]](#cite_note-276)^{#cite_ref-276}  
* [Abu Dhabi](/wiki/Abu_Dhabi "Abu Dhabi"), United Arab Emirates
* [Amman](/wiki/Amman "Amman"), Jordan
* [Baghdad](/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad"), Iraq
* [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing"), China
* [Damascus](/wiki/Damascus "Damascus"), Syria
* [East Jerusalem](/wiki/East_Jerusalem "East Jerusalem"), Palestine
* [Istanbul](/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul"), Turkey
* [Kairouan](/wiki/Kairouan "Kairouan"), Tunisia
* [Khartoum](/wiki/Khartoum "Khartoum"), Sudan
* [Muscat](/wiki/Muscat "Muscat"), Oman
* [Palermo Province](/wiki/Province_of_Palermo "Province of Palermo"), Italy
* [Rabat](/wiki/Rabat "Rabat"), Morocco
* [Sanaa](/wiki/Sanaa "Sanaa"), Yemen
* [Seoul](/wiki/Seoul "Seoul"), South Korea
* [Stuttgart](/wiki/Stuttgart "Stuttgart"), Germany
* [Tashkent](/wiki/Tashkent "Tashkent"), Uzbekistan
* [Tbilisi](/wiki/Tbilisi "Tbilisi"), Georgia
* [Tokyo](/wiki/Tokyo "Tokyo"), Japan
* [Tripoli, Libya](/wiki/Tripoli,_Libya "Tripoli, Libya")  

Notable people {#Notable_people}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: Notable people")\]

|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg) | This section **does not [cite](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources") any [sources](/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")** . * [Zulfikar family](/wiki/Zulfikar_family "Zulfikar family"), Egyptian noble family
* [Rabab Al-Kadhimi](/wiki/Rabab_Al-Kadhimi "Rabab Al-Kadhimi") (1918--1998), dentist and poet
* [Wael Alaa](/wiki/Neobyrd "Neobyrd") (born 1987), musician known as Neobyrd
* [Amr Aly](/wiki/Amr_Aly "Amr Aly") (born 1962), American soccer player and Olympian
* [Gamal Aziz](/wiki/Gamal_Aziz "Gamal Aziz"), also known as Gamal Mohammed Abdelaziz, former president and chief operating officer of [Wynn Resorts](/wiki/Wynn_Resorts "Wynn Resorts"), and former CEO of [MGM Resorts International](/wiki/MGM_Resorts_International "MGM Resorts International"), indicted as part of the [2019 college admissions bribery scandal](/wiki/2019_college_admissions_bribery_scandal "2019 college admissions bribery scandal")
* [Yasser Arafat](/wiki/Yasser_Arafat "Yasser Arafat") (1929--2004), born Mohammed Abdel Rahman Abdel Raouf al-Qudwa al-Husseini, was the 3rd Chairman of The [PLO](/wiki/Palestine_Liberation_Organization "Palestine Liberation Organization") and first president of the [Palestinian Authority](/wiki/Palestinian_National_Authority "Palestinian National Authority")
* [Abu Sa'id al-Afif](/wiki/Abu_Sa%27id_al-Afif "Abu Sa'id al-Afif"), 15th-century Samaritan
* [Ezz El-Dine Zulficar](/wiki/Ezz_El-Dine_Zulficar "Ezz El-Dine Zulficar"), (1919--1963) was an Egyptian film director, screenwriter, actor and producer, known for his distinctive style, which blends romance and action. Zulficar was one of the most influential filmmakers in the [Egyptian Cinema's](/wiki/Cinema_of_Egypt "Cinema of Egypt") golden age.
* [Boutros Ghali](/wiki/Boutros_Boutros-Ghali "Boutros Boutros-Ghali") (1922--2016), former [Secretary-General of the United Nations](/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations "Secretary-General of the United Nations")
* [Dalida](/wiki/Dalida "Dalida") (1933--1987), Italian-Egyptian singer who lived most of her life in France, received 55 golden records and was the first singer to receive a [diamond disc](/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification "Music recording sales certification")
* [Farouk El-Baz](/wiki/Farouk_El-Baz "Farouk El-Baz") (born 1938), an [Egyptian American](/wiki/Egyptian_American "Egyptian American") [space scientist](/wiki/Space_scientist "Space scientist") who worked with [NASA](/wiki/NASA "NASA") to assist in the planning of scientific exploration of the Moon, including the selection of landing sites for the Apollo missions and the training of astronauts in lunar observations and photography
* [Ahmed Mourad Bey Zulfikar](/wiki/Ahmed_Mourad_Bey_Zulfikar "Ahmed Mourad Bey Zulfikar") (1888--1945), Egyptian chief of police
* [Freddy Elbaiady](/wiki/Freddy_Elbaiady "Freddy Elbaiady") (born 1971), Egyptian politician
* [Mohamed ElBaradei](/wiki/Mohamed_ElBaradei "Mohamed ElBaradei") (born 1942), former [Director General](/wiki/Director-general "Director-general") of the [International Atomic Energy Agency](/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency "International Atomic Energy Agency"), [2005 Nobel Peace Prize laureate](/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize "Nobel Peace Prize")
* [C. S. Forester](/wiki/C._S._Forester "C. S. Forester") (1899--1966), English novelist known for writing tales of naval warfare, born in Cairo.
* [Nourane Foster](/wiki/Nourane_Fotsing_Moluh_Hassana "Nourane Fotsing Moluh Hassana") (born 1987), Cameroonian entrepreneur, politician and member of the National Assembly
* [William Donald Hamilton](/wiki/William_Donald_Hamilton "William Donald Hamilton") (1936--2000), British evolutionary biologist, was born in Cairo
* [Mauro Hamza](/wiki/Mauro_Hamza "Mauro Hamza") (born 1965 or 1966), fencing coach
* [Taco Hemingway](/wiki/Taco_Hemingway "Taco Hemingway") (born 1990), Polish hip-hop artist
* [Dorothy Hodgkin](/wiki/Dorothy_Hodgkin "Dorothy Hodgkin") (1910--1994), British chemist, credited with the development of [protein crystallography](/wiki/Protein_crystallography "Protein crystallography"), [Nobel Prize in Chemistry](/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry "Nobel Prize in Chemistry") in 1964
* [Naguib Mahfouz](/wiki/Naguib_Mahfouz "Naguib Mahfouz") (1911--2006), novelist, [Nobel Prize in Literature](/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature "Nobel Prize in Literature") laureate in 1988
* [Roland Moreno](/wiki/Roland_Moreno "Roland Moreno") (1945--2012), French inventor, engineer, humorist and author who invented the [smart card](/wiki/Smart_card "Smart card")
* [Gamal Abdel Nasser](/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser") (1918--1970) was an Egyptian politician who served as the [second President of Egypt](/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Egypt "List of Presidents of Egypt") from 1954 until his death in 1970.
* [Ahmed Sabri](/wiki/Ahmed_Sabri "Ahmed Sabri") (1889--1955), painter
* [Dina Zulfikar](/wiki/Dina_Zulfikar "Dina Zulfikar") (born 1962), film distributor and animal welfare activist
* [Mohamed Sobhi](/wiki/Mohamed_Sobhi_(actor) "Mohamed Sobhi (actor)") (born 1948), film, television and stage actor, and director
* [Blessed](/wiki/Beatification "Beatification") [Maria Caterina Troiani](/wiki/Maria_Caterina_Troiani "Maria Caterina Troiani") (1813--1887), a [charitable activist](/wiki/Mercy "Mercy")
* [Magdi Yacoub](/wiki/Magdi_Yacoub "Magdi Yacoub") (born 1935), Egyptian-British cardiothoracic surgeon
* [Hesham Youssef](/wiki/Hesham_Youssef "Hesham Youssef"), Egyptian diplomat
* [Ahmed Zulfikar](/wiki/Ahmed_Zulfikar "Ahmed Zulfikar") (1952--2010), mechanical engineer and entrepreneur
* [Naguib Sawiris](/wiki/Naguib_Sawiris "Naguib Sawiris") (born 1954), businessman, 62nd richest person on Earth in 2007 [list of billionaires](/wiki/Billionaire "Billionaire"), reaching US$10.0 billion with his company [Orascom Telecom Holding](/wiki/Orascom_Telecom_Holding "Orascom Telecom Holding")
* [Yakub Kadri Karaosmanoğlu](/wiki/Yakub_Kadri_Karaosmano%C4%9Flu "Yakub Kadri Karaosmanoğlu") (1889--1974), Turkish novelist
* [Mona Zulficar](/wiki/Mona_Zulficar "Mona Zulficar") (born 1950), lawyer and [human rights activist](/wiki/Human_rights_defender "Human rights defender"). She was included in the [Forbes](/wiki/Forbes "Forbes") 2021 list of the "100 most powerful businesswomen in the Arab region".
* [Ismail Pacha](/wiki/Isma%27il_Pasha_of_Egypt "Isma'il Pasha of Egypt") (1830--1895), was an Egyptian politician who served as [Khedive](/wiki/Khedive "Khedive") of [Egypt](/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt "Khedivate of Egypt") from 1863 to 1879
* [Avi Cohen](/wiki/Avi_Cohen "Avi Cohen") (1956--2010), Israeli international footballer

Explanatory notes {#Explanatory_notes}
--------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cairo&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: Explanatory notes")\]  
1. **[\^](#cite_ref-3)** Cairo Metropolitan is enlarged to cover all the area within the Governorate limits. Government statistics consider that the whole governorate is urban and the whole governorate is treated like as the metropolitan-city of Cairo. Governorate Cairo is considered a city-proper and functions as a municipality. The city of Alexandria is on the same principle as the city of Cairo, being a governorate-city. Because of this, it is difficult to divide Cairo into urban, rural, subdivisions, or to eliminate certain parts of the metropolitan administrative territory on various theme (unofficial statistics and data).{#cite_note-3}
{#cite_note-3}
2. **[\^](#cite_ref-32)** The historical chronicler [John of Nikiou](/wiki/John_of_Nikiou "John of Nikiou") attributed the construction of the fortress to Trajan, but more recent excavations date the fortress to the time of Diocletian. A succession of canals connecting the Nile Valley with the Red Sea were also previously dug around this region in different periods prior to Trajan. Trajan's canal fell out of use some time between the reign of Diocletian and the 7th century.{#cite_note-32}
{#cite_note-32}

* Jörg Armbruster, Suleman Taufiq (Eds.) *مدينتي القاهرة (MYCAI -- My Cairo Mein Kairo)* , text by different authors, photos by Barbara Armbruster and Hala Elkoussy, edition esefeld \& traub, Stuttgart 2014, [ISBN](/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-3-9809887-8-0](/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-9809887-8-0 "Special:BookSources/978-3-9809887-8-0").
